{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_013cEbvv8qXP9ZYzqW5VNion","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_012xsF96LbKarTBHGaVzm12p","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Diagnostic API provides a way for VS Code extensions to report code issues (errors, warnings, information, hints) to users within the editor. The API allows extensions to:\n\n- Create diagnostic collections to organize diagnostics by source (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint')\n- Report diagnostics for specific files or documents\n- Track and manage diagnostics across the workspace\n- Subscribe to diagnostic changes globally\n- Provide detailed diagnostic information with related locations and additional metadata\n\nDiagnostics are displayed in the editor gutter, problems panel, and inline as squiggles. They can be associated with quick fixes through the Code Actions API.\n\n## Core Types\n\n### DiagnosticSeverity\n\nEnum representing the severity level of a diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticSeverity {\n  Error = 0,\n  Warning = 1,\n  Information = 2,\n  Hint = 3\n}\n```\n\n**Members:**\n\n| Member | Value | Description |\n|--------|-------|-------------|\n| `Error` | 0 | Something not allowed by the rules of a language or other means. Used for errors that prevent compilation or execution. |\n| `Warning` | 1 | Something suspicious but allowed. Typically used for issues that won't prevent compilation but should be reviewed. |\n| `Information` | 2 | Something to inform about but not a problem. General informational messages. |\n| `Hint` | 3 | Something to hint at a better way of doing it, like proposing a refactoring. Used for code improvement suggestions. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Default severity when creating a `Diagnostic` without specifying severity is `Error`\n- Severity levels are used by VS Code for visualization (color, icon) and filtering in the Problems panel\n- Filtering priority when too many diagnostics are present: diagnostics are kept in order of severity (Error > Warning > Information > Hint)\n\n### DiagnosticTag\n\nEnum representing additional metadata about the type of a diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticTag {\n  Unnecessary = 1,\n  Deprecated = 2\n}\n```\n\n**Members:**\n\n| Member | Value | Description |\n|--------|-------|-------------|\n| `Unnecessary` | 1 | Unused or unnecessary code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered faded out. The opacity is controlled by the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\"` theme color (e.g., `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\": \"#000000c0\"` renders at 75% opacity). For high contrast themes, the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.border\"` theme color underlines unnecessary code instead. |\n| `Deprecated` | 2 | Deprecated or obsolete code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered with a strike-through. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Tags are optional and can be combined in an array\n- Tags provide visual feedback to users about the nature of the issue beyond just severity\n- Tags affect rendering but not the core behavior or filtering of diagnostics\n\n### DiagnosticRelatedInformation\n\nClass representing additional context for a diagnostic, pointing to related code locations that caused or are related to the diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport class DiagnosticRelatedInformation {\n  constructor(location: Location, message: string);\n  location: Location;\n  message: string;\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | The location of the related diagnostic information. Contains a URI and a Range pointing to the relevant code location. |\n| `message` | `string` | The human-readable message describing the related information. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Used to point to code locations that cause or relate to a diagnostic (e.g., when symbol names collide, all definitions can be marked)\n- Can be accessed by clicking on related information markers in the editor\n- Multiple related information items can be associated with a single diagnostic\n- Related information is particularly useful for complex diagnostics with multiple contributing factors\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\n// Pointing to duplicate symbol definitions\ndiagnostic.relatedInformation = [\n  new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n    new vscode.Location(uri, new vscode.Range(5, 0, 5, 10)),\n    'First declaration of symbol'\n  ),\n  new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n    new vscode.Location(uri, new vscode.Range(15, 0, 15, 10)),\n    'Second declaration of symbol'\n  )\n];\n```\n\n### Diagnostic\n\nClass representing a diagnostic, such as a compiler error or warning. Diagnostic objects are only valid in the scope of a file.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport class Diagnostic {\n  constructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity);\n  range: Range;\n  message: string;\n  severity: DiagnosticSeverity;\n  source?: string;\n  code?: string | number | { value: string | number; target: Uri };\n  relatedInformation?: DiagnosticRelatedInformation[];\n  tags?: DiagnosticTag[];\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Required | Description |\n|----------|------|----------|-------------|\n| `range` | `Range` | Yes | The range in the document to which this diagnostic applies. Defines the start and end position of the issue. |\n| `message` | `string` | Yes | The human-readable message describing the issue. Displayed to the user in the editor and problems panel. |\n| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity` | Yes (default: Error) | The severity level of the diagnostic. Default is `DiagnosticSeverity.Error`. |\n| `source` | `string?` | No | Human-readable string describing the source of this diagnostic (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint', 'super lint'). Useful for identifying which tool reported the issue. |\n| `code` | `string \\| number \\| { value: string \\| number; target: Uri }?` | No | A code or identifier for this diagnostic, used for later processing (e.g., when providing code actions). Can be a simple value or an object with a value and a target URI for additional information. |\n| `relatedInformation` | `DiagnosticRelatedInformation[]?` | No | Array of related diagnostic information pointing to related code locations (e.g., duplicate symbol definitions). |\n| `tags` | `DiagnosticTag[]?` | No | Additional metadata about the diagnostic. Can include `DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary` or `DiagnosticTag.Deprecated` to provide visual hints. |\n\n**Constructor Parameters:**\n\n| Parameter | Type | Description |\n|-----------|------|-------------|\n| `range` | `Range` | The range to which this diagnostic applies. |\n| `message` | `string` | The human-readable message. |\n| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity?` | The severity, default is `DiagnosticSeverity.Error`. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Diagnostics are immutable once retrieved from a collection; properties can only be modified before adding to a collection\n- A diagnostic is always scoped to a resource and a collection\n- Diagnostic messages support localization through the `l10n` API\n- When there are too many diagnostics per file, they are filtered by severity (Error > Warning > Information > Hint)\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst range = new vscode.Range(\n  new vscode.Position(0, 0),\n  new vscode.Position(0, 5)\n);\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Variable never used',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n);\ndiagnostic.source = 'eslint';\ndiagnostic.code = 'no-unused-vars';\ndiagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n```\n\n### DiagnosticChangeEvent\n\nInterface representing the event data fired when diagnostics change globally.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticChangeEvent {\n  readonly uris: readonly Uri[];\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `uris` | `readonly Uri[]` | An array of resources for which diagnostics have changed. This includes all URIs where diagnostics were added, modified, or removed. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Fired by the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event when diagnostics change in any collection\n- The event aggregates all changes across all diagnostic collections\n- URIs represent the documents where changes occurred\n- Empty arrays may be fired in some cases when clearing all diagnostics\n\n### DiagnosticCollection\n\nInterface representing a container for managing diagnostics. Diagnostics are always scoped to a collection and a resource.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticCollection extends Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]> {\n  readonly name: string;\n  set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void;\n  set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void;\n  delete(uri: Uri): void;\n  clear(): void;\n  forEach(callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any, thisArg?: any): void;\n  get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined;\n  has(uri: Uri): boolean;\n  dispose(): void;\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `name` | `string` (readonly) | The name of this diagnostic collection (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint'). Every diagnostic from this collection is associated with this name. The name is used by the task framework when defining problem matchers. |\n\n**Methods:**\n\n#### set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void\n**Description:** Assign diagnostics for the given resource. Will replace existing diagnostics for that resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - A resource identifier (URI).\n- `diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined` - Array of diagnostics or `undefined` to clear diagnostics for this URI.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Replaces all previous diagnostics for the given URI\n- Passing `undefined` is equivalent to calling `delete(uri)`\n- Fires the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event after setting diagnostics\n- Setting an empty array effectively clears diagnostics for the URI\n\n#### set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void\n**Description:** Replace diagnostics for multiple resources in this collection.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>` - Array of tuples like `[[file1, [d1, d2]], [file2, [d3, d4]]]`, or `undefined`.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Multiple tuples of the same URI are merged (e.g., `[[file1, [d1]], [file1, [d2]]]` is equivalent to `[[file1, [d1, d2]]]`)\n- If a diagnostics item is `undefined` as in `[file1, undefined]`, all previous diagnostics for that file are removed (but not subsequent ones)\n- More efficient than calling `set(uri, diagnostics)` multiple times as it batches updates\n- Fires a single `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event for all changed URIs\n- Results in a single synchronization with the main thread\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.set([\n  [uri1, [diag1, diag2]],\n  [uri2, [diag3]],\n  [uri3, undefined] // Clear diagnostics for uri3\n]);\n```\n\n#### delete(uri: Uri): void\n**Description:** Remove all diagnostics from this collection that belong to the provided URI. Equivalent to `set(uri, undefined)`.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - A resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Removes all diagnostics for the given URI\n- Fires the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event\n- If the URI has no diagnostics, this is a no-op\n\n#### clear(): void\n**Description:** Remove all diagnostics from this collection. Equivalent to calling `set(undefined)`.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Removes diagnostics for all resources in the collection\n- Fires the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event with all previously diagnosed URIs\n- After clearing, `forEach` will not iterate any entries\n- Useful for bulk cleanup when an extension no longer needs to report diagnostics\n\n#### forEach(callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any, thisArg?: any): void\n**Description:** Iterate over each entry in this collection.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any` - Function to execute for each entry. Receives the URI, the diagnostics array for that URI, and the collection itself.\n- `thisArg?: any` - Optional `this` context used when invoking the callback function.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- The diagnostics array passed to the callback is immutable (readonly)\n- Iteration order is not guaranteed\n- If the collection is modified during iteration, behavior is undefined\n- Useful for debugging or when you need to access all diagnostics at once\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.forEach((uri, diagnostics) => {\n  console.log(`${uri.fsPath}: ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n});\n```\n\n#### get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined\n**Description:** Get the diagnostics for a given resource. Note that you cannot modify the diagnostics array returned from this call.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - A resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:** `readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined` - An immutable array of diagnostics or `undefined` if no diagnostics exist for this URI.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Returns an immutable copy of the diagnostics array\n- Returns `undefined` (not an empty array) if the URI has no diagnostics\n- The returned array cannot be modified directly\n- Changes to diagnostics must be done through `set()` or `delete()`\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(uri);\nif (diagnostics) {\n  console.log(`Found ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n}\n```\n\n#### has(uri: Uri): boolean\n**Description:** Check if this collection contains diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - A resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:** `boolean` - `true` if this collection has diagnostics for the given resource, `false` otherwise.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Returns `true` only if `get(uri)` would return a non-undefined value\n- More efficient than calling `get(uri) !== undefined`\n\n#### dispose(): void\n**Description:** Dispose and free associated resources. Calls `clear()` internally.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Should be called when the extension no longer needs the collection\n- Automatically clears all diagnostics\n- After disposal, all methods will throw an error when called\n- Collections passed to `context.subscriptions.push()` are automatically disposed when the extension is deactivated\n- Failing to dispose can lead to memory leaks and continued reporting of diagnostics\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-extension');\n// ... use collection ...\ncollection.dispose(); // Clean up resources\n```\n\n## Functions\n\n### createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection\n\n**Description:** Create a new diagnostic collection.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport function createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection;\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n\n| Parameter | Type | Required | Description |\n|-----------|------|----------|-------------|\n| `name` | `string?` | No | The name of the collection. Every diagnostic from this collection will be associated with this name. Used by the task framework when defining problem matchers. If not provided, a unique name is generated. |\n\n**Returns:** `DiagnosticCollection` - A new diagnostic collection instance.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Each call creates a new, independent collection\n- Collections with the same name from different extensions will show diagnostics separately in the UI but can be aggregated programmatically\n- The name should be unique per extension to avoid confusion in the Problems panel\n- Collections should be cached if used repeatedly to avoid unnecessary allocations\n- Collections are not automatically disposed; you must call `dispose()` or add to `context.subscriptions`\n- Creating a collection is lightweight and doesn't immediately consume resources until diagnostics are added\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\ncollection.set(uri, [\n  new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Error message')\n]);\n```\n\n### getDiagnostics(resource?: Uri): Diagnostic[] | [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n\n**Description:** Get all diagnostics for a given resource, or all diagnostics across the workspace.\n\nThis function has two overloads:\n\n#### Overload 1: getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[]\n**Description:** Get all diagnostics for a given resource from all collections.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `resource: Uri` - A resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:** `Diagnostic[]` - An array of diagnostics objects or an empty array if no diagnostics exist for this resource.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Returns diagnostics from all collections for the given resource\n- Returns an empty array (not `undefined`) if the resource has no diagnostics\n- The returned array is mutable and independent from source collections\n- Useful for checking if a file has any issues regardless of which extension reported them\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\nconsole.log(`Found ${diagnostics.length} total diagnostics for this file`);\n```\n\n#### Overload 2: getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n**Description:** Get all diagnostics across the entire workspace.\n\n**Parameters:** None\n\n**Returns:** `[Uri, Diagnostic[]][]` - An array of uri-diagnostics tuples representing all diagnostics in the workspace or an empty array.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Returns aggregated diagnostics from all collections\n- Each entry is a tuple of `[Uri, Diagnostic[]]`\n- Returns an empty array if no diagnostics exist in the workspace\n- Can be computationally expensive on large workspaces with many diagnostics\n- The returned array is mutable and independent from source collections\n- Useful for workspace-wide analysis or exporting diagnostics\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst allDiagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\nlet errorCount = 0;\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of allDiagnostics) {\n  errorCount += diagnostics.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error).length;\n}\nconsole.log(`Total errors in workspace: ${errorCount}`);\n```\n\n## Events\n\n### onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>\n\n**Description:** An event which fires when the global set of diagnostics changes. This includes newly added and removed diagnostics.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport const onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>;\n```\n\n**Event Data:**\n- `DiagnosticChangeEvent` - Contains an array of URIs for which diagnostics have changed.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Fires whenever diagnostics are added, modified, or removed in any collection\n- Fires once per batch of changes (multiple `set()` calls in quick succession may be batched)\n- The event includes all URIs that were affected by the change\n- Changing severity, tags, or other properties of a diagnostic triggers this event\n- Clearing all diagnostics fires the event with all URIs that had diagnostics\n- Provides a global view of diagnostic changes across all extensions and collections\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nvscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n  for (const uri of event.uris) {\n    const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n    console.log(`Diagnostics changed for ${uri.fsPath}: ${diagnostics.length} total`);\n  }\n});\n```\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Example: Creating and Publishing Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('example');\n  context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n  // Listen to document changes\n  vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(event => {\n    const uri = event.document.uri;\n    const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n    // Example: Report diagnostics for lines containing \"todo\"\n    for (let i = 0; i < event.document.lineCount; i++) {\n      const line = event.document.lineAt(i);\n      const todoIndex = line.text.toLowerCase().indexOf('todo');\n\n      if (todoIndex !== -1) {\n        const range = new vscode.Range(\n          i,\n          todoIndex,\n          i,\n          todoIndex + 4\n        );\n        const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n          range,\n          'TODO: This needs to be completed',\n          vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Information\n        );\n        diagnostic.source = 'example';\n        diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n      }\n    }\n\n    // Update diagnostics for this file\n    collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n  }, null, context.subscriptions);\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Diagnostics with Related Information\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('symbol-checker');\n  context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n  async function checkSymbolDuplicates(document: vscode.TextDocument) {\n    const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n    const symbolMap = new Map<string, vscode.Range[]>();\n\n    // Find all symbol declarations (simplified example)\n    for (let i = 0; i < document.lineCount; i++) {\n      const line = document.lineAt(i);\n      const match = line.text.match(/\\bclass\\s+(\\w+)/);\n\n      if (match) {\n        const symbol = match[1];\n        const range = new vscode.Range(\n          i,\n          match.index!,\n          i,\n          match.index! + match[0].length\n        );\n\n        if (!symbolMap.has(symbol)) {\n          symbolMap.set(symbol, []);\n        }\n        symbolMap.get(symbol)!.push(range);\n      }\n    }\n\n    // Report duplicates with related information\n    for (const [symbol, ranges] of symbolMap.entries()) {\n      if (ranges.length > 1) {\n        for (const range of ranges) {\n          const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n            range,\n            `Duplicate symbol '${symbol}'`,\n            vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n          );\n          diagnostic.source = 'symbol-checker';\n\n          // Point to all other declarations\n          diagnostic.relatedInformation = ranges\n            .filter(r => r !== range)\n            .map(r => new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n              new vscode.Location(document.uri, r),\n              'Other declaration'\n            ));\n\n          diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n        }\n      }\n    }\n\n    collection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n  }\n\n  // Check on document open and change\n  vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(checkSymbolDuplicates, null, context.subscriptions);\n  vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(e => checkSymbolDuplicates(e.document), null, context.subscriptions);\n}\n```\n\n### Example: Clearing Diagnostics When Extension Deactivates\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nlet diagnosticCollection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection;\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  diagnosticCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-extension');\n\n  // ... rest of activation code ...\n\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnosticCollection);\n}\n\nexport function deactivate() {\n  // Collection is automatically disposed via context.subscriptions\n  // Or explicitly: diagnosticCollection.dispose();\n}\n```\n\n### Example: Bulk Update with Multiple Files\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('bulk-checker');\n  context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n  async function checkAllFiles() {\n    const files = await vscode.workspace.findFiles('**/*.js');\n    const entries: [vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[]][] = [];\n\n    for (const uri of files) {\n      const document = await vscode.workspace.openTextDocument(uri);\n      const diagnostics = checkDocument(document);\n\n      if (diagnostics.length > 0) {\n        entries.push([uri, diagnostics]);\n      } else {\n        // Clear diagnostics for this file\n        entries.push([uri, []]);\n      }\n    }\n\n    // Update all at once (more efficient than individual set() calls)\n    collection.set(entries);\n  }\n\n  // Trigger on activation\n  checkAllFiles();\n}\n\nfunction checkDocument(document: vscode.TextDocument): vscode.Diagnostic[] {\n  // Implementation...\n  return [];\n}\n```\n\n### Example: Listening to Diagnostic Changes\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const diagnosticWatcher = vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n    console.log('Diagnostics changed for:');\n    for (const uri of event.uris) {\n      const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning).length;\n\n      console.log(`  ${uri.fsPath}: ${errors} errors, ${warnings} warnings`);\n    }\n  });\n\n  context.subscriptions.push(diagnosticWatcher);\n}\n```\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: Diagnostic Collection as a Service\n\n```typescript\n// diagnosticService.ts\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport class DiagnosticService {\n  private readonly collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection;\n\n  constructor(name: string) {\n    this.collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection(name);\n  }\n\n  public report(uri: vscode.Uri, diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[]): void {\n    this.collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n  }\n\n  public clear(uri?: vscode.Uri): void {\n    if (uri) {\n      this.collection.delete(uri);\n    } else {\n      this.collection.clear();\n    }\n  }\n\n  public dispose(): void {\n    this.collection.dispose();\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: Debounced Diagnostic Updates\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('debounced');\n  let timeout: NodeJS.Timeout | undefined;\n\n  const updateDiagnostics = (document: vscode.TextDocument) => {\n    // Clear previous timeout\n    if (timeout) clearTimeout(timeout);\n\n    // Set new timeout to debounce rapid changes\n    timeout = setTimeout(() => {\n      const diagnostics = performExpensiveCheck(document);\n      collection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }, 500); // Wait 500ms after user stops typing\n  };\n\n  vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(e => updateDiagnostics(e.document), null, context.subscriptions);\n  context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n}\n\nfunction performExpensiveCheck(document: vscode.TextDocument): vscode.Diagnostic[] {\n  // Implementation...\n  return [];\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Language-Specific Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport class LanguageDiagnosticsManager {\n  private collections: Map<string, vscode.DiagnosticCollection> = new Map();\n\n  public getCollection(language: string): vscode.DiagnosticCollection {\n    if (!this.collections.has(language)) {\n      this.collections.set(language, vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection(language));\n    }\n    return this.collections.get(language)!;\n  }\n\n  public reportForLanguage(language: string, uri: vscode.Uri, diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[]): void {\n    this.getCollection(language).set(uri, diagnostics);\n  }\n\n  public dispose(): void {\n    for (const collection of this.collections.values()) {\n      collection.dispose();\n    }\n    this.collections.clear();\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 4: Filtering by Severity\n\n```typescript\nconst allDiagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n\n// Get only errors\nconst errors = allDiagnostics.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error);\n\n// Get errors and warnings\nconst important = allDiagnostics.filter(d =>\n  d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error ||\n  d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n);\n\n// Get by source\nconst typescriptDiags = allDiagnostics.filter(d => d.source === 'typescript');\n```\n\n### Pattern 5: Code with Complex Information\n\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Unused variable');\ndiagnostic.code = {\n  value: 'no-unused-vars',\n  target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-unused-vars')\n};\ndiagnostic.source = 'eslint';\n```\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Accessing Disposed Collections\n\n**Error:** Methods called on a disposed `DiagnosticCollection` will throw an error.\n\n**Handling:**\n```typescript\ntry {\n  collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n} catch (error) {\n  console.error('Collection is disposed');\n}\n```\n\n**Prevention:**\n- Store the collection reference and reuse it\n- Avoid disposing collections while still in use\n- Use try-finally or context.subscriptions for automatic cleanup\n\n### Invalid URI Handling\n\n**Behavior:** Invalid URIs are typically silently ignored or cause errors when used with diagnostics.\n\n**Prevention:**\n```typescript\n// Validate URIs before use\nif (!uri || !uri.scheme || !uri.fsPath) {\n  console.warn('Invalid URI');\n  return;\n}\n\ncollection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n```\n\n### Handling Undefined Results\n\n**Behavior:** `get(uri)` returns `undefined`, not an empty array, when no diagnostics exist.\n\n**Correct handling:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(uri);\nif (diagnostics) {\n  // Process diagnostics\n  console.log(`Found ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n} else {\n  console.log('No diagnostics for this file');\n}\n```\n\n### Memory Leaks from Undisposed Collections\n\n**Problem:** Collections not properly disposed continue to retain diagnostics and consume memory.\n\n**Prevention:**\n```typescript\n// ✓ Good: Add to subscriptions for automatic disposal\ncontext.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n// ✓ Good: Explicitly dispose\ncollection.dispose();\n\n// ✗ Bad: No disposal\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection();\n// ... collection is never disposed\n```\n\n### Performance Considerations\n\n**Issues:**\n- Very large diagnostic arrays (1000+) per file can impact editor performance\n- `getDiagnostics()` without parameters on large workspaces is expensive\n- Frequent collection updates can cause flickering\n\n**Mitigation:**\n```typescript\n// Limit diagnostics per file if needed\nconst MAX_DIAGNOSTICS = 1000;\nif (diagnostics.length > MAX_DIAGNOSTICS) {\n  diagnostics = diagnostics.slice(0, MAX_DIAGNOSTICS);\n  // Notify user of truncation\n}\n\n// Batch updates\ncollection.set([[uri1, diags1], [uri2, diags2], [uri3, diags3]]);\n\n// Debounce updates on rapid changes\n// See \"Debounced Diagnostic Updates\" pattern above\n```\n\n### Related Information Validation\n\n**Issue:** Invalid related information locations cause errors.\n\n**Validation:**\n```typescript\nconst relatedInformation = diagnostic.relatedInformation || [];\nfor (const info of relatedInformation) {\n  // Ensure location has valid URI and range\n  if (!info.location?.uri || !info.location?.range) {\n    console.warn('Invalid related information location');\n    continue;\n  }\n  // Use validated info...\n}\n```\n\n## API Lifecycle and Resource Management\n\n### Extension Activation and Deactivation\n\n```typescript\n// Extension is activated when first used\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-extension');\n\n  // IMPORTANT: Add to subscriptions for automatic cleanup\n  context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n  // Extension is deactivated when VS Code shuts down or extension is disabled\n}\n\n// Called when extension is deactivated\nexport function deactivate() {\n  // All subscriptions are automatically disposed\n}\n```\n\n### Collection Lifecycle\n\n1. **Creation**: `createDiagnosticCollection()` creates a new collection\n2. **Usage**: Set/update diagnostics with `set()`, `delete()`, `clear()`\n3. **Disposal**: Call `dispose()` or add to `context.subscriptions`\n4. **After disposal**: All methods throw errors\n\n### Best Practices\n\n- Always add collections to `context.subscriptions` for automatic cleanup\n- Reuse collection instances rather than creating new ones repeatedly\n- Clear diagnostics before deactivation if appropriate\n- Use event handlers to subscribe/unsubscribe appropriately\n- Validate all URIs and ranges before creating diagnostics\n- Consider performance when reporting large numbers of diagnostics\n\n## Interoperability\n\n### With Code Actions API\n\nDiagnostics can be associated with code actions:\n\n```typescript\nvscode.languages.registerCodeActionsProvider(selector, {\n  provideCodeActions(document, range, context) {\n    // context.diagnostics contains diagnostics affecting this range\n    return context.diagnostics\n      .filter(d => d.code === 'specific-error')\n      .map(d => createFixFor(d));\n  }\n});\n```\n\n### With Problem Matchers\n\nThe diagnostic collection name is used by VS Code's task system:\n- Task problem matchers can reference diagnostic collection names\n- Named collections appear in the Problems panel grouped by source\n\n### With Language Server Protocol\n\nExtensions using LSP typically:\n1. Receive diagnostics from the language server\n2. Convert them to VS Code `Diagnostic` objects\n3. Report them via diagnostic collections\n\n```typescript\n// Example: TypeScript language features\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  message,\n  severity\n);\ndiagnostic.source = 'typescript';\ndiagnostic.code = { value: code, target: uri };\ncollection.set(fileUri, [diagnostic]);\n```\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":431,"cache_read_input_tokens":67207,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":431},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a1a6ed46-4b1d-4344-86e8-6e46bad2754e","uuid":"7d9d2fbc-eb2f-4b7e-a2ff-90feff364b16"}

The API allows extensions to:\n\n- Create diagnostic collections to organize diagnostics by source (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint')\n- Report diagnostics for specific files or documents\n- Track and manage diagnostics across the workspace\n- Subscribe to diagnostic changes globally\n- Provide detailed diagnostic information with related locations and additional metadata\n\nDiagnostics are displayed in the editor gutter, problems panel, and inline as squiggles. They can be associated with quick fixes through the Code Actions API.\n\n## Core Types\n\n### DiagnosticSeverity\n\nEnum representing the severity level of a diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticSeverity {\n  Error = 0,\n  Warning = 1,\n  Information = 2,\n  Hint = 3\n}\n```\n\n**Members:**\n\n| Member | Value | Description |\n|--------|-------|-------------|\n| `Error` | 0 | Something not allowed by the rules of a language or other means. Used for errors that prevent compilation or execution. |\n| `Warning` | 1 | Something suspicious but allowed. Typically used for issues that won't prevent compilation but should be reviewed. |\n| `Information` | 2 | Something to inform about but not a problem. General informational messages. |\n| `Hint` | 3 | Something to hint at a better way of doing it, like proposing a refactoring. Used for code improvement suggestions. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Default severity when creating a `Diagnostic` without specifying severity is `Error`\n- Severity levels are used by VS Code for visualization (color, icon) and filtering in the Problems panel\n- Filtering priority when too many diagnostics are present: diagnostics are kept in order of severity (Error > Warning > Information > Hint)\n\n### DiagnosticTag\n\nEnum representing additional metadata about the type of a diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticTag {\n  Unnecessary = 1,\n  Deprecated = 2\n}\n```\n\n**Members:**\n\n| Member | Value | Description |\n|--------|-------|-------------|\n| `Unnecessary` | 1 | Unused or unnecessary code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered faded out. The opacity is controlled by the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\"` theme color (e.g., `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\": \"#000000c0\"` renders at 75% opacity). For high contrast themes, the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.border\"` theme color underlines unnecessary code instead. |\n| `Deprecated` | 2 | Deprecated or obsolete code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered with a strike-through. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Tags are optional and can be combined in an array\n- Tags provide visual feedback to users about the nature of the issue beyond just severity\n- Tags affect rendering but not the core behavior or filtering of diagnostics\n\n### DiagnosticRelatedInformation\n\nClass representing additional context for a diagnostic, pointing to related code locations that caused or are related to the diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport class DiagnosticRelatedInformation {\n  constructor(location: Location, message: string);\n  location: Location;\n  message: string;\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `location` | `Location` | The location of the related diagnostic information. Contains a URI and a Range pointing to the relevant code location. |\n| `message` | `string` | The human-readable message describing the related information. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Used to point to code locations that cause or relate to a diagnostic (e.g., when symbol names collide, all definitions can be marked)\n- Can be accessed by clicking on related information markers in the editor\n- Multiple related information items can be associated with a single diagnostic\n- Related information is particularly useful for complex diagnostics with multiple contributing factors\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\n// Pointing to duplicate symbol definitions\ndiagnostic.relatedInformation = [\n  new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n    new vscode.Location(uri, new vscode.Range(5, 0, 5, 10)),\n    'First declaration of symbol'\n  ),\n  new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n    new vscode.Location(uri, new vscode.Range(15, 0, 15, 10)),\n    'Second declaration of symbol'\n  )\n];\n```\n\n### Diagnostic\n\nClass representing a diagnostic, such as a compiler error or warning. Diagnostic objects are only valid in the scope of a file.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport class Diagnostic {\n  constructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity);\n  range: Range;\n  message: string;\n  severity: DiagnosticSeverity;\n  source?: string;\n  code?: string | number | { value: string | number; target: Uri };\n  relatedInformation?: DiagnosticRelatedInformation[];\n  tags?: DiagnosticTag[];\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Required | Description |\n|----------|------|----------|-------------|\n| `range` | `Range` | Yes | The range in the document to which this diagnostic applies. Defines the start and end position of the issue. |\n| `message` | `string` | Yes | The human-readable message describing the issue. Displayed to the user in the editor and problems panel. |\n| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity` | Yes (default: Error) | The severity level of the diagnostic. Default is `DiagnosticSeverity.Error`. |\n| `source` | `string?` | No | Human-readable string describing the source of this diagnostic (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint', 'super lint'). Useful for identifying which tool reported the issue. |\n| `code` | `string \\| number \\| { value: string \\| number; target: Uri }?` | No | A code or identifier for this diagnostic, used for later processing (e.g., when providing code actions). Can be a simple value or an object with a value and a target URI for additional information. |\n| `relatedInformation` | `DiagnosticRelatedInformation[]?` | No | Array of related diagnostic information pointing to related code locations (e.g., duplicate symbol definitions). |\n| `tags` | `DiagnosticTag[]?` | No | Additional metadata about the diagnostic. Can include `DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary` or `DiagnosticTag.Deprecated` to provide visual hints. |\n\n**Constructor Parameters:**\n\n| Parameter | Type | Description |\n|-----------|------|-------------|\n| `range` | `Range` | The range to which this diagnostic applies. |\n| `message` | `string` | The human-readable message. |\n| `severity` | `DiagnosticSeverity?` | The severity, default is `DiagnosticSeverity.Error`. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Diagnostics are immutable once retrieved from a collection; properties can only be modified before adding to a collection\n- A diagnostic is always scoped to a resource and a collection\n- Diagnostic messages support localization through the `l10n` API\n- When there are too many diagnostics per file, they are filtered by severity (Error > Warning > Information > Hint)\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst range = new vscode.Range(\n  new vscode.Position(0, 0),\n  new vscode.Position(0, 5)\n);\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n  range,\n  'Variable never used',\n  vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n);\ndiagnostic.source = 'eslint';\ndiagnostic.code = 'no-unused-vars';\ndiagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n```\n\n### DiagnosticChangeEvent\n\nInterface representing the event data fired when diagnostics change globally.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticChangeEvent {\n  readonly uris: readonly Uri[];\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `uris` | `readonly Uri[]` | An array of resources for which diagnostics have changed. This includes all URIs where diagnostics were added, modified, or removed. |\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Fired by the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event when diagnostics change in any collection\n- The event aggregates all changes across all diagnostic collections\n- URIs represent the documents where changes occurred\n- Empty arrays may be fired in some cases when clearing all diagnostics\n\n### DiagnosticCollection\n\nInterface representing a container for managing diagnostics. Diagnostics are always scoped to a collection and a resource.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticCollection extends Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]> {\n  readonly name: string;\n  set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void;\n  set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void;\n  delete(uri: Uri): void;\n  clear(): void;\n  forEach(callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any, thisArg?: any): void;\n  get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined;\n  has(uri: Uri): boolean;\n  dispose(): void;\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n| Property | Type | Description |\n|----------|------|-------------|\n| `name` | `string` (readonly) | The name of this diagnostic collection (e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint'). Every diagnostic from this collection is associated with this name. The name is used by the task framework when defining problem matchers. |\n\n**Methods:**\n\n#### set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void\n**Description:** Assign diagnostics for the given resource. Will replace existing diagnostics for that resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - A resource identifier (URI).\n- `diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined` - Array of diagnostics or `undefined` to clear diagnostics for this URI.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Replaces all previous diagnostics for the given URI\n- Passing `undefined` is equivalent to calling `delete(uri)`\n- Fires the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event after setting diagnostics\n- Setting an empty array effectively clears diagnostics for the URI\n\n#### set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void\n**Description:** Replace diagnostics for multiple resources in this collection.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>` - Array of tuples like `[[file1, [d1, d2]], [file2, [d3, d4]]]`, or `undefined`.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Multiple tuples of the same URI are merged (e.g., `[[file1, [d1]], [file1, [d2]]]` is equivalent to `[[file1, [d1, d2]]]`)\n- If a diagnostics item is `undefined` as in `[file1, undefined]`, all previous diagnostics for that file are removed (but not subsequent ones)\n- More efficient than calling `set(uri, diagnostics)` multiple times as it batches updates\n- Fires a single `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event for all changed URIs\n- Results in a single synchronization with the main thread\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.set([\n  [uri1, [diag1, diag2]],\n  [uri2, [diag3]],\n  [uri3, undefined] // Clear diagnostics for uri3\n]);\n```\n\n#### delete(uri: Uri): void\n**Description:** Remove all diagnostics from this collection that belong to the provided URI. Equivalent to `set(uri, undefined)`.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - A resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Removes all diagnostics for the given URI\n- Fires the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event\n- If the URI has no diagnostics, this is a no-op\n\n#### clear(): void\n**Description:** Remove all diagnostics from this collection. Equivalent to calling `set(undefined)`.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Removes diagnostics for all resources in the collection\n- Fires the `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event with all previously diagnosed URIs\n- After clearing, `forEach` will not iterate any entries\n- Useful for bulk cleanup when an extension no longer needs to report diagnostics\n\n#### forEach(callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any, thisArg?: any): void\n**Description:** Iterate over each entry in this collection.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any` - Function to execute for each entry. Receives the URI, the diagnostics array for that URI, and the collection itself.\n- `thisArg?: any` - Optional `this` context used when invoking the callback function.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- The diagnostics array passed to the callback is immutable (readonly)\n- Iteration order is not guaranteed\n- If the collection is modified during iteration, behavior is undefined\n- Useful for debugging or when you need to access all diagnostics at once\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.forEach((uri, diagnostics) => {\n  console.log(`${uri.fsPath}: ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n});\n```\n\n#### get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined\n**Description:** Get the diagnostics for a given resource. Note that you cannot modify the diagnostics array returned from this call.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - A resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:** `readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined` - An immutable array of diagnostics or `undefined` if no diagnostics exist for this URI.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Returns an immutable copy of the diagnostics array\n- Returns `undefined` (not an empty array) if the URI has no diagnostics\n- The returned array cannot be modified directly\n- Changes to diagnostics must be done through `set()` or `delete()`\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(uri);\nif (diagnostics) {\n  console.log(`Found ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n}\n```\n\n#### has(uri: Uri): boolean\n**Description:** Check if this collection contains diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri: Uri` - A resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:** `boolean` - `true` if this collection has diagnostics for the given resource, `false` otherwise.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Returns `true` only if `get(uri)` would return a non-undefined value\n- More efficient than calling `get(uri) !== undefined`\n\n#### dispose(): void\n**Description:** Dispose and free associated resources. Calls `clear()` internally.\n\n**Returns:** void\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Should be called when the extension no longer needs the collection\n- Automatically clears all diagnostics\n- After disposal, all methods will throw an error when called\n- Collections passed to `context.subscriptions.push()` are automatically disposed when the extension is deactivated\n- Failing to dispose can lead to memory leaks and continued reporting of diagnostics\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-extension');\n// ... use collection ...\ncollection.dispose(); // Clean up resources\n```\n\n## Functions\n\n### createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection\n\n**Description:** Create a new diagnostic collection.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport function createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection;\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n\n| Parameter | Type | Required | Description |\n|-----------|------|----------|-------------|\n| `name` | `string?` | No | The name of the collection. Every diagnostic from this collection will be associated with this name. Used by the task framework when defining problem matchers. If not provided, a unique name is generated. |\n\n**Returns:** `DiagnosticCollection` - A new diagnostic collection instance.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Each call creates a new, independent collection\n- Collections with the same name from different extensions will show diagnostics separately in the UI but can be aggregated programmatically\n- The name should be unique per extension to avoid confusion in the Problems panel\n- Collections should be cached if used repeatedly to avoid unnecessary allocations\n- Collections are not automatically disposed; you must call `dispose()` or add to `context.subscriptions`\n- Creating a collection is lightweight and doesn't immediately consume resources until diagnostics are added\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\ncollection.set(uri, [\n  new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Error message')\n]);\n```\n\n### getDiagnostics(resource?: Uri): Diagnostic[] | [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n\n**Description:** Get all diagnostics for a given resource, or all diagnostics across the workspace.\n\nThis function has two overloads:\n\n#### Overload 1: getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[]\n**Description:** Get all diagnostics for a given resource from all collections.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `resource: Uri` - A resource identifier.\n\n**Returns:** `Diagnostic[]` - An array of diagnostics objects or an empty array if no diagnostics exist for this resource.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Returns diagnostics from all collections for the given resource\n- Returns an empty array (not `undefined`) if the resource has no diagnostics\n- The returned array is mutable and independent from source collections\n- Useful for checking if a file has any issues regardless of which extension reported them\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\nconsole.log(`Found ${diagnostics.length} total diagnostics for this file`);\n```\n\n#### Overload 2: getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n**Description:** Get all diagnostics across the entire workspace.\n\n**Parameters:** None\n\n**Returns:** `[Uri, Diagnostic[]][]` - An array of uri-diagnostics tuples representing all diagnostics in the workspace or an empty array.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Returns aggregated diagnostics from all collections\n- Each entry is a tuple of `[Uri, Diagnostic[]]`\n- Returns an empty array if no diagnostics exist in the workspace\n- Can be computationally expensive on large workspaces with many diagnostics\n- The returned array is mutable and independent from source collections\n- Useful for workspace-wide analysis or exporting diagnostics\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst allDiagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\nlet errorCount = 0;\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of allDiagnostics) {\n  errorCount += diagnostics.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error).length;\n}\nconsole.log(`Total errors in workspace: ${errorCount}`);\n```\n\n## Events\n\n### onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>\n\n**Description:** An event which fires when the global set of diagnostics changes. This includes newly added and removed diagnostics.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport const onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>;\n```\n\n**Event Data:**\n- `DiagnosticChangeEvent` - Contains an array of URIs for which diagnostics have changed.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Fires whenever diagnostics are added, modified, or removed in any collection\n- Fires once per batch of changes (multiple `set()` calls in quick succession may be batched)\n- The event includes all URIs that were affected by the change\n- Changing severity, tags, or other properties of a diagnostic triggers this event\n- Clearing all diagnostics fires the event with all URIs that had diagnostics\n- Provides a global view of diagnostic changes across all extensions and collections\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nvscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n  for (const uri of event.uris) {\n    const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n    console.log(`Diagnostics changed for ${uri.fsPath}: ${diagnostics.length} total`);\n  }\n});\n```\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Example: Creating and Publishing Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('example');\n  context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n  // Listen to document changes\n  vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(event => {\n    const uri = event.document.uri;\n    const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n    // Example: Report diagnostics for lines containing \"todo\"\n    for (let i = 0; i < event.document.lineCount; i++) i,\n          todoIndex,\n          i,\n          todoIndex + 4\n        );\n        const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n          range,\n          'TODO: This needs to be completed',\n          vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Information\n        );\n        diagnostic.source = 'example';\n        diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n      }\n    }\n\n    // Update diagnostics for this file\n    collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n  }, null, context.subscriptions);\n}\n```\n\n### Advanced Example: Diagnostics with Related Information\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('symbol-checker');\n  context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n  async function checkSymbolDuplicates(document: vscode.TextDocument) {\n    const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n    const symbolMap = new Map<string, vscode.Range[]>();\n\n    // Find all symbol declarations (simplified example)\n    for (let i = 0; i < document.lineCount; i++) {\n      const line = document.lineAt(i);\n      const match = line.text.match(/\\bclass\\s+(\\w+)/);\n\n      if (match) {\n        const symbol = match[1];\n        const range = new vscode.Range(\n          i,\n          match.index!,\n          i,\n          match.index! + match[0].length\n        );\n\n        if (!symbolMap.has(symbol)) {\n          symbolMap.set(symbol, []);\n        }\n        symbolMap.get(symbol)!.push(range);\n      }\n    }\n\n    // Report duplicates with related information\n    for (const [symbol, ranges] of symbolMap.entries()) {\n      if (ranges.length > 1) {\n        for (const range of ranges) {\n          const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n            range,\n            `Duplicate symbol '${symbol}'`,\n            vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n          );\n          diagnostic.source = 'symbol-checker';\n\n          // Point to all other declarations\n          diagnostic.relatedInformation = ranges\n            .filter(r => r !== range)\n            .map(r => new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n              new vscode.Location(document.uri, r),\n              'Other declaration'\n            ));\n\n          diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n        }\n      }\n    }\n\n    collection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n  }\n\n  // Check on document open and change\n  vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(checkSymbolDuplicates, null, context.subscriptions);\n  vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(e => checkSymbolDuplicates(e.document), null, context.subscriptions);\n}\n```\n\n### Example: Clearing Diagnostics When Extension vscode.workspace.openTextDocument(uri);\n      const diagnostics = checkDocument(document);\n\n      if (diagnostics.length > 0) {\n        entries.push([uri, diagnostics]);\n      } else {\n        // Clear diagnostics for this file\n        entries.push([uri, []]);\n      }\n    }\n\n    // Update all at once (more efficient than individual set() calls)\n    collection.set(entries);\n  }\n\n  // Trigger on activation\n  checkAllFiles();\n}\n\nfunction checkDocument(document: vscode.TextDocument): vscode.Diagnostic[] {\n  // Implementation...\n  return [];\n}\n```\n\n### Example: Listening to Diagnostic Changes\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const diagnosticWatcher = 'vscode';\n\nexport class DiagnosticService {\n  private readonly collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection;\n\n  constructor(name: string) {\n    this.collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection(name);\n  }\n\n  public report(uri: vscode.Uri, diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[]): void {\n    this.collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n  }\n\n  public clear(uri?: vscode.Uri): void {\n    if (uri) {\n      this.collection.delete(uri);\n    } else {\n      this.collection.clear();\n    }\n  }\n\n  public dispose(): void {\n    this.collection.dispose();\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: Debounced Diagnostic Updates\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('debounced');\n  let timeout: NodeJS.Timeout | undefined;\n\n  const updateDiagnostics = (document: vscode.TextDocument) => {\n    // Clear previous timeout\n    if (timeout) clearTimeout(timeout);\n\n    // Set new timeout to debounce rapid changes\n    timeout = setTimeout(() => {\n      const diagnostics = performExpensiveCheck(document);\n      collection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }, 500); // Wait 500ms after user stops typing\n  };\n\n  vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(e => updateDiagnostics(e.document), null, context.subscriptions);\n  context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n}\n\nfunction performExpensiveCheck(document: vscode.TextDocument): vscode.Diagnostic[] {\n  // Implementation...\n  return [];\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Language-Specific Diagnostics\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport class LanguageDiagnosticsManager {\n  private collections: Map<string, vscode.DiagnosticCollection> = new Map();\n\n  public getCollection(language: string): vscode.DiagnosticCollection {\n    if (!this.collections.has(language)) {\n      this.collections.set(language, vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection(language));\n    }\n    return this.collections.get(language)!;\n  }\n\n  public reportForLanguage(language: string, uri: vscode.Uri, diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[]): void {\n    this.getCollection(language).set(uri, diagnostics);\n  }\n\n  public dispose(): void {\n    for (const collection of this.collections.values()) {\n      collection.dispose();\n    }\n    this.collections.clear();\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 4: Filtering by Severity\n\n```typescript\nconst allDiagnostics = allDiagnostics.filter(d =>\n  d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error ||\n  d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n);\n\n// Get by source\nconst typescriptDiags = allDiagnostics.filter(d => d.source === 'typescript');\n```\n\n### Pattern 5: Code with Complex Information\n\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, 'Unused variable');\ndiagnostic.code = {\n  value: 'no-unused-vars',\n  target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://eslint.org/docs/rules/no-unused-vars')\n};\ndiagnostic.source = 'eslint';\n```\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Accessing Disposed Collections\n\n**Error:** Methods called on a disposed `DiagnosticCollection` will throw an error.\n\n**Handling:**\n```typescript\ntry {\n  collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n} catch (error) {\n  console.error('Collection is disposed');\n}\n```\n\n**Prevention:**\n- Store the collection reference and reuse it\n- Avoid disposing collections while still in use\n- Use try-finally or context.subscriptions for automatic cleanup\n\n### Invalid URI Handling\n\n**Behavior:** Invalid URIs are typically silently ignored or cause errors when used with diagnostics.\n\n**Prevention:**\n```typescript\n// Validate URIs before use\nif (!uri || !uri.scheme || !uri.fsPath) {\n  console.warn('Invalid URI');\n  return;\n}\n\ncollection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n```\n\n### Handling Undefined Results\n\n**Behavior:** `get(uri)` returns `undefined`, not an empty array, when no diagnostics exist.\n\n**Correct handling:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(uri);\nif (diagnostics) {\n  // Process diagnostics\n  console.log(`Found ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n} else {\n  console.log('No diagnostics for this file');\n}\n```\n\n### Memory Leaks from Undisposed Collections\n\n**Problem:** Collections not properly disposed continue to retain diagnostics and consume memory.\n\n**Prevention:**\n```typescript\n// ✓ Good: Add to subscriptions for automatic disposal\ncontext.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n// ✓ Good: Explicitly dispose\ncollection.dispose();\n\n// ✗ Bad: No disposal\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection();\n// ... collection is never disposed\n```\n\n### Performance Considerations\n\n**Issues:**\n- Very large diagnostic arrays (1000+) per file can impact editor performance\n- `getDiagnostics()` without parameters on large workspaces is expensive\n- Frequent collection updates can cause flickering\n\n**Mitigation:**\n```typescript\n// Limit diagnostics per file if needed\nconst MAX_DIAGNOSTICS = 1000;\nif (diagnostics.length > MAX_DIAGNOSTICS) {\n  diagnostics = diagnostics.slice(0, MAX_DIAGNOSTICS);\n  // Notify user of truncation\n}\n\n// Batch updates\ncollection.set([[uri1, diags1], [uri2, diags2], [uri3, diags3]]);\n\n// Debounce updates on rapid changes\n// See \"Debounced Diagnostic Updates\" pattern above\n```\n\n### Related Information Validation\n\n**Issue:** Invalid related information locations cause errors.\n\n**Validation:**\n```typescript\nconst relatedInformation = diagnostic.relatedInformation || [];\nfor (const info of relatedInformation) {\n  // Ensure location has valid URI and range\n  if (!info.location?.uri || !info.location?.range) {\n    console.warn('Invalid related information location');\n    continue;\n  }\n  // Use validated info...\n}\n```\n\n## API Lifecycle and Resource Management\n\n### Extension Activation and Deactivation\n\n```typescript\n// Extension is activated when first used\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n  const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-extension');\n\n  // IMPORTANT: Add to subscriptions for automatic cleanup\n  context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n  // Extension is deactivated when VS Code shuts down or extension is disabled\n}\n\n// Called when extension is deactivated\nexport function deactivate() {\n  // All subscriptions are automatically disposed\n}\n```\n\n### Collection Lifecycle\n\n1. **Creation**: `createDiagnosticCollection()` creates a new collection\n2. **Usage**: Set/update diagnostics with `set()`, `delete()`, `clear()`\n3. **Disposal**: Call `dispose()` or add to `context.subscriptions`\n4. **After disposal**: All methods throw errors\n\n### Best Practices\n\n- Always add collections to `context.subscriptions` for automatic cleanup\n- Reuse collection instances rather than creating new ones repeatedly\n- Clear diagnostics before deactivation if appropriate\n- Use event handlers to subscribe/unsubscribe appropriately\n- Validate all URIs and ranges before creating diagnostics\n- Consider performance when reporting large numbers of diagnostics\n\n## Interoperability\n\n### With Code Actions API\n\nDiagnostics can be associated with code actions:\n\n```typescript\nvscode.languages.registerCodeActionsProvider(selector, {\n  provideCodeActions(document, range, context) {\n    // context.diagnostics contains diagnostics affecting this range\n    return context.diagnostics\n      .filter(d => d.code === 'specific-error')\n      .map(d => createFixFor(d));\n  }\n});\n```\n\n### With Problem Matchers\n\nThe diagnostic collection name is used by VS Code's task system:\n- Task problem matchers can reference diagnostic collection names\n- Named collections appear in the Problems panel grouped by source\n\n### With Language Server Protocol\n\nExtensions using LSP typically:\n1.
